## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, rate laws typically express dA/dt as power-law or rational functions of concentration, with time-dependence appearing in photochemistry, catalyst deactivation, or externally driven reactions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (reaction with constant source/sink term)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with inhibition)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or activation)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first and second order pathways)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Fractional order with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 + t)**c3 (diffusion-limited kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer power-law dependence on concentration → elementary reaction step with molecularity equal to the power
- Rational function of concentration (A/(K+A)) → enzyme or surface-catalyzed mechanism with site saturation
- Product of concentration and (constant - concentration) → autocatalytic or logistic growth mechanism
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel competing reaction pathways
- Fractional (non-integer) power of concentration → complex mechanism or diffusion-controlled kinetics
- Negative sign on leading term → consumption/decay of reactant species
- Denominator with squared concentration term → substrate or product inhibition mechanism
- Exponential dependence on time multiplied by concentration → time-varying rate constant (catalyst aging, temperature ramp)
- Square root of concentration (A**0.5) → dissociative equilibrium preceding rate-limiting step
- Rate independent of A but dependent on t → zero-order kinetics with externally controlled driving force

**GT:** `-0.11493*A**2 + 0.06807*A*log(0.25693*t + 1)`

This has two terms:
1. A term proportional to `A²`
2. A term proportional to `A*log(linear_in_t)`

Let me analyze candidates systematically, looking for ones that can produce `A²` and `A*log(...)` terms.

**Key observations about GT structure:**
- It's a sum of `c*A²` and `c*A*log(c*t + 1)`
- No constant offset, no exponential terms, no other powers of A

Let me check candidates that have `A²` and logarithmic terms:

**Candidate 3:** `A*c0*(c1+t)**c2 + A*c3 + A**c4*c5`
- Set c4=2: gives `A*c0*(c1+t)**c2 + A*c3 + c5*A²`
- The `A²` term works. But `A*c0*(c1+t)**c2` — can `(c1+t)**c2` become `log(c*t+1)`? No, a power function can't equal a logarithm for all t.

**Candidate 4:** `A*c0*(c1+t)**c2 + A*c3 + A**c4*c5 + c6`
Same issue — power vs log.

**Candidates 10, 33, 40:** These contain `log(c*t + 1)` terms explicitly!

**Candidate 10:** `A*c0*(c1+t)**(1/3) + A**c2*c3 + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6*log(c7*t+1) + c8*t + c9`

- Same issue: log term lacks A factor. **No match.**

- Again, log term lacks A. **No match.**

**Candidate 35:** `A*c0*(c1+t)**c2 + A**c3*c4 + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*log(A*c8+1)`

**GT: -0.11493·A² + 0.06807·A·log(0.25693·t + 1)**

This has two terms:
1. A term proportional to A²
2. A term proportional to A·log(linear function of t)

Note that A·log(c₃t + c₄) can be rewritten. The key structural requirement is having an A² term and an A·log(linear in t) term, with all other terms zeroed out.

Let me also note that log(c₃t + c₄) = log(c₄(c₃t/c₄ + 1)) = log(c₄) + log(c₃t/c₄ + 1). So A·log(c₃t + c₄) = A·log(c₄) + A·log(c₃/c₄·t + 1). The A·log(c₄) part is just a constant times A.

So GT = -0.11493·A² + const₁·A + const₂·A·log(const₃·t + 1)

Now I need to check if any candidate can produce exactly this form. The critical basis functions needed are: **A²** and **A·log(linear in t)**.

Let me check which candidates have a log term or a power-law term (c+t)^c that could become log.

**Key insight**: (c+t)^c cannot become log(c+t) for any constant c. These are fundamentally different functions. A power function and a logarithm are linearly independent. So I need candidates that explicitly contain a logarithmic term in t, or can produce one.

Let me scan for candidates with log terms involving t:

- **Candidate 10**: has c₆·log(c₇t+1) but also A·c₀·(c₁+t)^(1/3) — the A·log term isn't multiplied by A properly. The log term is c₆·log(c₇t+1), not A·log(...). Would need A times log, but the log term here has no A factor. [NO MATCH]

- **Candidate 14**: A·c₀·(c₁+t)^(1/3) + A^c₂·c₃ + A^c₄·c₅ + c₆·log(c₇t+1) + c₈t + c₉. Log not multiplied by A. [NO MATCH]

None of the candidates have A·log(t-expression) as a term.

Now, could any rational function in t exactly equal log(t+const)? No — log is transcendental and cannot be represented by rational functions or power functions or exponentials.

Could (c+t)^c with c→0 give log? Only in a limit, which is forbidden by Rule 2.

Let me verify there are truly no candidates with A·log(f(t)). Scanning all candidates... None have A multiplied by a log of a t-expression.

Some candidates have log(A·c + 1) terms (Candidates 19, 23, 32, 35, 38, 44, 46) but these are log in A, not in t.
